Readyz health checks, on the other hand, have no grace period,\n// since readyz should fail until boot fully completes.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddBootSequenceHealthChecks(checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.addHealthChecks(s.livezGracePeriod, checks...)\n}\n\n// addHealthChecks adds health checks to healthz, livez, and readyz. The delay passed in will set\n// a corresponding grace period on livez.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) addHealthChecks(livezGracePeriod time.Duration, checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\tif err := s.healthzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif err := s.livezRegistry.addDelayedHealthChecks(livezGracePeriod, checks...); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn s.readyzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...)\n}\n\n// AddReadyzChecks allows you to add a HealthCheck to readyz.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddReadyzChecks(checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.readyzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...)\n}\n\n// AddLivezChecks allows you to add a HealthCheck to livez.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddLivezChecks(delay time.Duration, checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.livezRegistry.addDelayedHealthChecks(delay, checks...)\n}\n\n// addReadyzShutdownCheck is a convenience function for adding a readyz shutdown check, so\n// that we can register that the api-server is no longer ready while we attempt to gracefully\n// shutdown.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) addReadyzShutdownCheck(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n\treturn s.AddReadyzChecks(healthz.NewShutdownHealthz(stopCh))\n}\n\n// installHealthz creates the healthz endpoint for this server\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installHealthz() {\n\ts.healthzRegistry.installHandler(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux)\n}\n\n// installReadyz creates the readyz endpoint for this server.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installReadyz() {\n\ts.readyzRegistry.installHandlerWithHealthyFunc(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux, func() {\n\t\t// note: installHandlerWithHealthyFunc guarantees that this is called only once\n\t\ts.lifecycleSignals.HasBeenReady.Signal()\n\t})\n}\n\n// installLivez creates the livez endpoint for this server.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installLivez() {\n\ts.livezRegistry.installHandler(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux)\n}\n\n// delayedHealthCheck wraps a health check which will not fail until the explicitly defined delay has elapsed. This\n// is intended for use primarily for livez health checks.\nfunc delayedHealthCheck(check healthz.HealthChecker, clock clock.Clock, delay time.Duration) healthz.HealthChecker {\n\treturn delayedLivezCheck{\n\t\tcheck,\n\t\tclock.Now().Add(delay),\n\t\tclock,\n\t}\n}","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":168}}}

\"text\": \"## Health Check Endpoint Implementations Across Kubernetes, Grafana, and Prometheus\\n\\n### Kubernetes\\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz.go` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/healthz.go`\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated health check system with three endpoints:\\n- `/healthz` - Returns 200 when server is running (backwards compatibility)\\n- `/livez` - Liveness probe indicating process is alive with configurable grace period\\n- `/readyz` - Readiness probe indicating server has completed boot and can handle traffic\\n\\nThe implementation uses a `healthCheckRegistry` struct that manages health checkers for each endpoint. Key components:\\n- `HealthChecker` interface with `Name()` and `Check(*http.Request) error` methods\\n- `PingHealthz` - Always returns healthy\\n- `LogHealthz` - Checks if logging subsystem is not blocked (must flush every 2 minutes)\\n- `NewInformerSyncHealthz()` - Checks if all informer caches have synced\\n- `NewShutdownHealthz()` - Fails when shutdown signal received\\n- `AddHealthChecks()` - Adds checks to all three endpoints\\n- `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()` - Adds checks with grace period for livez\\n- `AddReadyzChecks()` - Adds checks specific to readyz endpoint\\n\\nETCD storage health is verified via `EtcdHealthCheck()` function in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/healthcheck.go` which decodes etcd's health status JSON.\\n\\nController-manager at `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` uses `NewMutableHealthzHandler` from the controller-manager library and adds per-controller health checkers through the `HealthCheckAdder` interface. Each controller registers a `NamedHealthChecker` that tracks the controller's operational status.\\n\\n### Grafana\\n**Location**: `pkg/api/http_server.go` and `pkg/server/health.go`\\n\\nGrafana implements a simpler health check system:\\n\\n1. **Lightweight Endpoints**:\\n   - `/healthz` - Returns 200 with \\\"Ok\\\" if web server is running (no checks)\\n   - `/livez` - Always returns 200 (simple liveness indicator)\\n   - `/readyz` - Returns 200 if `HealthNotifier.IsReady()` is true, else 503 Service Unavailable\\n   - `/api/health` - Extended health endpoint that checks database connectivity\\n\\n2. **Health Tracking**:\\n   - `HealthNotifier` struct uses `atomic.Bool` for thread-safe readiness state\\n   - `SetReady()` and `SetNotReady()` methods allow operators to signal readiness\\n   - `IsReady()` returns current ready state\\n   - `LivezHandler()` always returns 200 OK\\n   - `ReadyzHandler()` depends on HealthNotifier state\\n\\n3. **Database Checks**:\\n   - `apiHealthHandler` at `/api/health` attempts database access and returns 503 if unavailable\\n   - Returns version information unless anonymous mode hides version\\n\\n4. **Registration**:\\n   - `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` registers `/livez` and `/readyz` on mux.Router\\n   - `healthzHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/healthz` requests\\n   - `apiHealthHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/api/health` requests\\n\\n### Prometheus\\n**Location**: `web/web.go`\\n\\nPrometheus uses the simplest approach with startup-state-aware endpoints:\\n\\n1. **Endpoints**:\\n   - `/-/healthy` - Liveness probe, always returns 200 with message \\\"{AppName} is Healthy.\\\"\\n   - `/-/ready` - Readiness probe wrapped with `testReady()` middleware\\n   - Both support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n2. **Ready State Management**:\\n   - `ReadyStatus` enum: `NotReady (0)`, `Ready (1)`, `Stopping (2)`\\n   - Stored in atomic field `h.ready`\\n   - `isReady()` method checks if status == Ready\\n\\n3. **Ready Wrapper**:\\n   - `testReady(f http.HandlerFunc)` wraps handlers to enforce readiness\\n   - Returns 200 OK with handler output if `Ready`\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with \\\"Service Unavailable\\\" message if `NotReady` or `Stopping`\\n   - Sets header `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true/false` to distinguish shutdown state\\n\\n4. **Usage**:\\n   - Federation endpoint (`/federate`), consoles, and other sensitive operations use `readyf()` wrapper\\n   - Metrics endpoint (`/metrics`) is always available regardless of ready state\\n   - Version endpoint (`/version`) is always available\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Complexity**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus\\n2. **Dependency Checks**: \\n   - Kubernetes: ETcd/storage, informer sync, logging, graceful shutdown\\n   - Grafana: Database connectivity via `/api/health`\\n   - Prometheus: Simple startup completion flag\\n3. **Grace Periods**: Only Kubernetes implements configurable grace periods for liveness probes\\n4. **Endpoint Naming**:\\n   - Kubernetes: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n   - Grafana: `/healthz`, `/api/health`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n   - Prometheus: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready`\\n5. **Architecture**: Kubernetes uses pluggable checker interfaces, Grafana uses explicit handlers, Prometheus uses state-based wrappers\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":43,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3282,"cache_read_input_tokens":65650,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3282},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bc5ccbdf-cc70-47ce-97c0-c0f018f55bb0","uuid":"688538ad-e597-452e-920e-62bd41ad57ec"}

`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/healthz.go`\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated health check system with three endpoints:\\n- `/healthz` - Returns 200 when server is running (backwards compatibility)\\n- `/livez` - Liveness probe indicating process is alive with configurable grace period\\n- `/readyz` - Readiness probe indicating server has completed boot and can handle traffic\\n\\nThe implementation uses a `healthCheckRegistry` struct that manages health checkers for each endpoint. Key components:\\n- `HealthChecker` interface with `Name()` and `Check(*http.Request) error` methods\\n- `PingHealthz` - Always returns healthy\\n- `LogHealthz` - Checks if logging subsystem is not blocked (must flush every 2 minutes)\\n- `NewInformerSyncHealthz()` - Checks if all informer caches have synced\\n- `NewShutdownHealthz()` - Fails when shutdown signal received\\n- `AddHealthChecks()` - Adds checks to all three endpoints\\n- `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()` - Adds checks with grace period for livez\\n- `AddReadyzChecks()` - Adds checks specific to readyz endpoint\\n\\nETCD storage health is verified via `EtcdHealthCheck()` function in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/healthcheck.go` which decodes etcd's health status JSON.\\n\\nController-manager at `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` uses `NewMutableHealthzHandler` from the controller-manager library and adds per-controller health checkers through the `HealthCheckAdder` interface. Each controller registers a `NamedHealthChecker` that tracks the controller's operational status.\\n\\n### Grafana\\n**Location**: `pkg/api/http_server.go` and `pkg/server/health.go`\\n\\nGrafana implements a simpler health check system:\\n\\n1. **Lightweight Endpoints**:\\n   - `/healthz` - Returns 200 with \\\"Ok\\\" if web server is running (no checks)\\n   - `/livez` - Always returns 200 (simple liveness indicator)\\n   - `/readyz` - Returns 200 if `HealthNotifier.IsReady()` is true, else 503 Service Unavailable\\n   - `/api/health` - Extended health endpoint that checks database connectivity\\n\\n2. **Health Tracking**:\\n   - `HealthNotifier` struct uses `atomic.Bool` for thread-safe readiness state\\n   - `SetReady()` and `SetNotReady()` methods allow operators to signal readiness\\n   - `IsReady()` returns current ready state\\n   - `LivezHandler()` always returns 200 OK\\n   - `ReadyzHandler()` depends on HealthNotifier state\\n\\n3. **Database Checks**:\\n   - `apiHealthHandler` at `/api/health` attempts database access and returns 503 if unavailable\\n   - Returns version information unless anonymous mode hides version\\n\\n4. **Registration**:\\n   - `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` registers `/livez` and `/readyz` on mux.Router\\n   - `healthzHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/healthz` requests\\n   - `apiHealthHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/api/health` requests\\n\\n### Prometheus\\n**Location**: `web/web.go`\\n\\nPrometheus uses the simplest approach with startup-state-aware endpoints:\\n\\n1. **Endpoints**:\\n   - `/-/healthy` - Liveness probe, always returns 200 with message \\\"{AppName} is Healthy.\\\"\\n   - `/-/ready` - Readiness probe wrapped with `testReady()` middleware\\n   - Both support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n2. **Ready State Management**:\\n   - `ReadyStatus` enum: `NotReady (0)`, `Ready (1)`, `Stopping (2)`\\n   - Stored in atomic field `h.ready`\\n   - `isReady()` method checks if status == Ready\\n\\n3. **Ready Wrapper**:\\n   - `testReady(f http.HandlerFunc)` wraps handlers to enforce readiness\\n   - Returns 200 OK with handler output if `Ready`\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with \\\"Service Unavailable\\\" message if `NotReady` or `Stopping`\\n   - Sets header `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true/false` to distinguish shutdown state\\n\\n4. **Usage**:\\n   - Federation endpoint (`/federate`), consoles, and other sensitive operations use `readyf()` wrapper\\n   - Metrics endpoint (`/metrics`) is always available regardless of ready state\\n   - Version endpoint (`/version`) is always available\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Complexity**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus\\n2. **Dependency Checks**: \\n   - Kubernetes: ETcd/storage, informer sync, logging, graceful shutdown\\n   - Grafana: Database connectivity via `/api/health`\\n   - Prometheus: Simple startup completion flag\\n3. **Grace Periods**: Only Kubernetes implements configurable grace periods for liveness probes\\n4. **Endpoint Naming**:\\n   - \"text\": \"## Health Check Endpoint Implementations Across Kubernetes, Grafana, and Prometheus\\n\\n### Kubernetes\\n**Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz.go` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/healthz.go`\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated health check system with three endpoints:\\n- `/healthz` - Returns 200 when server is running (backwards compatibility)\\n- `/livez` - Liveness probe indicating process is alive with configurable grace period\\n- `/readyz` - Readiness probe indicating server has completed boot and can handle traffic\\n\\nThe implementation uses a `healthCheckRegistry` struct that manages health checkers for each endpoint. Key components:\\n- `HealthChecker` interface with `Name()` and `Check(*http.Request) error` methods\\n- `PingHealthz` - Always returns healthy\\n- `LogHealthz` - Checks if logging subsystem is not blocked (must flush every 2 minutes)\\n- `NewInformerSyncHealthz()` - Checks if all informer caches have synced\\n- `NewShutdownHealthz()` - Fails when shutdown signal received\\n- `AddHealthChecks()` - Adds checks to all three endpoints\\n- `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()` - Adds checks with grace period for livez\\n- `AddReadyzChecks()` - Adds checks specific to readyz endpoint\\n\\nETCD storage health is verified via `EtcdHealthCheck()` function in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/healthcheck.go` which decodes etcd's health status JSON.\\n\\nController-manager at `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` uses `NewMutableHealthzHandler` from the controller-manager library and adds per-controller health checkers through the `HealthCheckAdder` interface. Each controller registers a `NamedHealthChecker` that tracks the controller's operational status.\\n\\n### Grafana\\n**Location**: `pkg/api/http_server.go` and `pkg/server/health.go`\\n\\nGrafana implements a simpler health check system:\\n\\n1. **Lightweight Endpoints**:\\n   - `/healthz` - Returns 200 with \\\"Ok\\\" if web server is running (no checks)\\n   - `/livez` - Always returns 200 (simple liveness indicator)\\n   - `/readyz` - Returns 200 if `HealthNotifier.IsReady()` is true, else 503 Service Unavailable\\n   - `/api/health` - Extended health endpoint that checks database connectivity\\n\\n2. **Health Tracking**:\\n   - `HealthNotifier` struct uses `atomic.Bool` for thread-safe readiness state\\n   - `SetReady()` and `SetNotReady()` methods allow operators to signal readiness\\n   - `IsReady()` returns current ready state\\n   - `LivezHandler()` always returns 200 OK\\n   - `ReadyzHandler()` depends on HealthNotifier state\\n\\n3. **Database Checks**:\\n   - `apiHealthHandler` at `/api/health` attempts database access and returns 503 if unavailable\\n   - Returns version information unless anonymous mode hides version\\n\\n4. **Registration**:\\n   - `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` registers `/livez` and `/readyz` on mux.Router\\n   - `healthzHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/healthz` requests\\n   - `apiHealthHandler()` is middleware that intercepts `/api/health` requests\\n\\n### Prometheus\\n**Location**: `web/web.go`\\n\\nPrometheus uses the simplest approach with startup-state-aware endpoints:\\n\\n1. **Endpoints**:\\n   - `/-/healthy` - Liveness probe, always returns 200 with message \\\"{AppName} is Healthy.\\\"\\n   - `/-/ready` - Readiness probe wrapped with `testReady()` middleware\\n   - Both support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n2. **Ready State Management**:\\n   - `ReadyStatus` enum: `NotReady (0)`, `Ready (1)`, `Stopping (2)`\\n   - Stored in atomic field `h.ready`\\n   - `isReady()` method checks if status == Ready\\n\\n3. **Ready Wrapper**:\\n   - `testReady(f http.HandlerFunc)` wraps handlers to enforce readiness\\n   - Returns 200 OK with handler output if `Ready`\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with \\\"Service Unavailable\\\" message if `NotReady` or `Stopping`\\n   - Sets header `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true/false` to distinguish shutdown state\\n\\n4. **Usage**:\\n   - Federation endpoint (`/federate`), consoles, and other sensitive operations use `readyf()` wrapper\\n   - Metrics endpoint (`/metrics`) is always available regardless of ready state\\n   - Version endpoint (`/version`) is always available\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Complexity**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus\\n2. **Dependency Checks**: \\n   - Kubernetes: ETcd/storage, informer sync, logging, graceful shutdown\\n   - Grafana: Database connectivity via `/api/health`\\n   - Prometheus: Simple startup completion flag\\n3. **Grace Periods**: Only Kubernetes implements configurable grace periods for liveness probes\\n4. **Endpoint Naming**:\\n   - Kubernetes: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n   - Grafana: `/healthz`, `/api/health`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n   - Prometheus: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready`\\n5. **Architecture**: Kubernetes uses pluggable checker interfaces, Grafana uses explicit handlers, Prometheus uses state-based wrappers\"\n}\n","numLines":168,"startLine":1,"totalLines":168}}}
